                  <hi rend="ital">A well-known kind of plant,</hi> (S, M, * K,) <hi rend="ital">of which the kind of paper termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قِرْطَاس</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">is made;</hi> (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">قرطس</foreign>, q. v. ;) [namely, <hi rend="ital">papyrus;</hi> and] <hi rend="ital">of which mats are made;</hi> (Msb;) [app. meaning <hi rend="ital">rushes</hi> in general: but the former is generally meant by it in the present day, and is probably the proper signification: anciently, mats, as well as ropes and sails &amp;c., were made of the rind of the papyrus; and even small boats were constructed of its stalks bound together; and of such, probably, was the ark in which the infant Moses was exposed: it is a coll. gen. n.:] n. un. <foreign lang="ar">بَرْدِيَّةٌ</foreign>. (M, TA.) Hence, <foreign lang="ar">قَطْنُ البَرْدِىّ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The cotton of the papyrus, which, resembling wool, is gathered from the stalk, and, mixed with lime, composes a very tenacious kind of cement.</hi> (Golius, from Ibn-Maaroof.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Also, a rel. n. from the same, meaning <hi rend="ital">Of,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">belonging to,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">resembling, the plant so called.</hi> Hence the saying,] <foreign lang="ar">لَهَا سَاقٌ بَرْدِيَّةٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">She has a shank like a papyrus-stalk</hi>].                   </form>, (S, M, &amp;c.,) with kesr (S, Mgh, K) to the <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign> and the <foreign lang="ar">ر</foreign> (Mgh, TA,) [in the CK <foreign lang="ar">اِبْرَدَة</foreign>,] <hi rend="ital">Cold in the belly,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">inside;</hi> (M, K;) <hi rend="ital">a well-known malady, arising from the prevalence of cold and humidity, and preventing one, by languor, from performing the act of coition:</hi> (S, Mgh:) and <hi rend="ital">a dripping of the urine, which prevents a man's taking pleasure in women.</hi> (T, L.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">Coldness</hi> of the damp earth, and of rain. (M, L.) An Arab says, <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّهَا لَبَارِدَةٌ اليَوْمَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Verily it</hi> (the morning, <foreign lang="ar">الغَدَاةُ</foreign>, L) <hi rend="ital">is cold to-day</hi>]; and another says to him, <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَتْ بِبَارِدَةٍ إِنَّمَا هِىَ إِبْرِدَةُ الثَّرَى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">It is not cold: it is only the coldness of the damp earth</hi>]. (S, L.)    </entryFree>35:T4b6,<entryFree id="n2241" key="مَبْرَدَةٌ" type="main">

                  </form> [<hi rend="ital">A cause of coldness</hi> or <hi rend="ital">coolness</hi>]. You say, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا الشَّىْءُ مَبْرَدَةٌ لِلْبَدَنِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">This thing is a cause of coldness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">coolness, to the body</hi>]: and As relates that he said to an Arab of the desert, “What induceth thee to take a sleep in the morning while the sun is yet low?” and he answered, <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّهَا مَبْرَدَةٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فِى الصَّيْفِ مَسْخَنَةٌ فِى الشِّتَآءِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Verily it is a cause of coolness in the summer,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">a cause of warmth in the winter</hi>].
